   continuous forest, forest fragments and cattle pastures in a landscape

LA English
C1 [Navarrete, Dario] El Colegio Frontera Sur, San Cristobal de las Casa 29290, Chiapas, Mexico.
   [Navarrete, Dario; Halffter, Gonzalo] Inst Ecol AC, Xalapa 91070, Veracruz, Mexico.
RP Navarrete, D (reprint author), El Colegio Frontera Sur, Carretera Panamer & Perifer Sur, San Cristobal de las Casa 29290, Chiapas, Mexico.
EM dnavarre@ecosur.mx
FU Comision Nacional para el uso y Conocimiento de la Biodiversidad [BE012,
   EE005]; Consejo Nacional de Ciencia y Tecnologia (CONACYT)
   [2004-CO1-56]; ORCYT-UNESCO [883.612.2]; WWF [RM16]
FX We want to thank Jorge Leon Cortes from El Colegio de la Frontera Sur
   and Vinicio Sosa from Instituto de Ecologia A. C. for their valuable
   comments and suggestions regarding this work; Leonardo Delgado from
   Instituto de Ecologia A. C., Fernando Vaz de Mello and David Edmonds for
   their help in the identification of specimens; Natura A. C. an its staff
   for their support during our stay in the Chajul Biological Station,
   especially to Gilberto and Armando Mendez, who assisted us during our
   field work. Ingrid Quintero and Gonzalo Halffter lent us the original
   text from their unpublished manuscript "Changes through time of the
   perturbation caused by modification and fragmentation of the tropical
   rain forest in an animal group ( Insecta: Coleoptera Scarabaeinae)''.
   Esther Quintero translated the text to English. We also want to thank
   the thorough and useful comments by two anonymous reviewers. Financial
   support for this work came from the Comision Nacional para el uso y
   Conocimiento de la Biodiversidad ( CONABIO, grants BE012, EE005),
   Consejo Nacional de Ciencia y Tecnologia (CONACYT) - Secretaria del
   Medio Ambiente y Recursos Naturales ( CONACYT - SEMARNAT project
   2004-CO1-56, ORCYT-UNESCO, project 883.612.2). Dario Navarrete wishes to
   thank CONACyT for a doctoral fellowship which was pursued at the
   Instituto de Ecologia A. C. Xalapa, Veracruz, Mexico, and to the WWF for
   the Professional Development Grant received by the RM16.

   Dahma farm kindly allowed us to work on their properties. J.A.P.
   Sumares, P. A. P. Antiqueira, H.J. Almeida and A. P. S. Perez helped in
   the fieldwork. C. Vieira was supported by an undergraduate fellowship
   from Fundacao de Amparo a Pesquisa do Estado de Sao Paulo (FAPESP, proc.
   no. 07/50716-1); G. Q. Romero was supported by a research grant from

   04/13658-5). This study was awarded (best poster presentation of
   undergraduate student) during the 17th International Congress of
